## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt is determined by nonlinear restoring forces (functions of x), damping terms (functions of v), and possibly external time-dependent driving forces. Classical nonlinear oscillator models like Duffing, van der Pol, and Rayleigh oscillators provide the structural templates.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple harmonic oscillator)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear damping plus restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (nonlinear damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear damping)
- Quintic Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinear restoring force)
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic external driving force)
- Parametrically driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) + c2 * v (parametric excitation)
- Softening spring with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v**2 + c2 * v (position-velocity coupling)
- Nonlinear damping with restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * x**2 + c2 * v**3 (combined van der Pol and Rayleigh)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (quadratic nonlinearity / asymmetric potential)
- General polynomial restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (asymmetric Duffing with damping)
- Coulomb-damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (c2 + x**2)**(-1) (nonlinear friction model)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric potential wells; even powers (x**2) → asymmetric potentials
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v → linear energy dissipation or gain (linear damping/driving)
- Products x**2 * v → amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of van der Pol type self-oscillation
- Cubic velocity terms v**3 → Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping that limits large-amplitude oscillations
- Explicit time dependence via sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) → external periodic driving force causing forced oscillations or resonance
- Parametric terms like x*cos(c*t) → parametric resonance where the effective spring constant is modulated in time
- Sign of cubic coefficient in x**3: positive → hardening spring (frequency increases with amplitude); negative → softening spring
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system; presence suggests non-autonomous driven dynamics

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (PO12)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - beta*Abs(v)**c1 - omega0**c2*(gamma*t + c3)*x - omega0**c4*x
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to analyze whether any candidate formula can match the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.0494*v³ - 1.0293*x*(0.0223*t + 1) - 1.0293*x + 0.4155*sin(t) - 0.2917*|v|^(1/3)`

Let me simplify the GT:
- `-0.0494*v³` — cubic in v
- `-1.0293*x*(0.0223*t + 1) - 1.0293*x` = `-1.0293*x*0.0223*t - 1.0293*x - 1.0293*x` = `-0.02295*x*t - 2.0586*x`
- `0.4155*sin(t)`
- `-0.2917*|v|^(1/3)`

So GT = `-0.0494*v³ - 0.02295*x*t - 2.0586*x + 0.4155*sin(t) - 0.2917*|v|^(1/3)`

Key features of the GT:
1. **v³ term**
2. **x*t term** (product of x and t)
3. **Linear x term**
4. **sin(t) term**
5. **|v|^(1/3) term** — involves absolute value of v raised to 1/3 power

The critical difficulty: The GT contains an **x*t** cross-term and an **|v|^(1/3)** term.

**x*t term analysis:** None of the candidates explicitly contain an `x*t` term. However, some use `tanh(c1*x + c2)` which, for small arguments, approximates `c1*x + c2 - (c1*x+c2)³/3 + ...`. This can't produce an `x*t` term.

Some candidates use `exp(c4*x²)*sin(c5*t + c6)` — when c4=0, this becomes `sin(c5*t + c6)`, which doesn't give `x*t`.

**|v|^(1/3) term analysis:** This is a fractional power of the absolute value of v. None of the candidates contain `|v|` or `Abs(v)` terms. The candidates contain terms like `v`, `v²`, `v³`, `v²*x`, `v*x`, `v*x²`, `log(...)`, `sqrt(...)`, etc. None can produce `|v|^(1/3)`.

Even if we could somehow approximate other terms, the `|v|^(1/3)` term is fundamentally non-analytic at v=0 and has a specific sign-symmetric behavior (|v|^(1/3) is always positive regardless of v's sign). No combination of polynomial terms in v (like v, v², v³) or other analytic functions can replicate this behavior.

Similarly, the `x*t` cross-term cannot be generated by any of the candidate structures. Let me check if any candidate has a structure that could produce `x*t`:
- `tanh(c1*x)` doesn't involve t
- `sin(c5*t)` doesn't involve x (when exp(c4*x²) has c4=0)
- `x*cos(c8*t)` in candidate 1 — this gives x*cos(t), not x*t

None of the candidates can produce both the `x*t` term and the `|v|^(1/3)` term simultaneously. Even ignoring the `|v|^(1/3)` term (which we cannot do since its coefficient is significant at -0.2917), no candidate can match.

Let me verify: could any candidate approximate `|v|^(1/3)` with some other term? Since this is about exact mathematical equivalence (not approximation), and since `|v|^(1/3)` is a non-analytic, non-polynomial function that's always non-negative and even in v, no candidate term can replicate it exactly.

After careful analysis of all 50 candidates, none can simultaneously produce:
1. The `x*t` cross-term

GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - beta*Abs(v)**c1 - omega0**c2*(gamma*t + c3)*x - omega0**c4*x

I need to analyze whether any candidate can exactly match the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.0494*v³ - 1.0293*x*(0.0223*t + 1) - 1.0293*x + 0.4155*sin(t) - 0.2917*|v|^(1/3)`

Simplifying the GT:
- `-0.0494*v³` — cubic in v
- `-1.0293*x*(0.0223*t + 1) - 1.0293*x` = `-1.0293*0.0223*t*x - 1.0293*x - 1.0293*x` = `-0.02294*t*x - 2.0586*x`
- `0.4155*sin(t)`
- `-0.2917*|v|^(1/3)`

So GT = `-0.0494*v³ - 0.02294*t*x - 2.0586*x + 0.4155*sin(t) - 0.2917*|v|^(1/3)`

The key basis functions in GT are:
1. `v³`
2. `t*x` (product of t and x)
3. `x` (linear)
4. `sin(t)`
5. `|v|^(1/3)` (cube root of absolute value of v)

This is critical: the GT contains `|v|^(1/3)` and `t*x` terms. Let me check each candidate for these.

**Key observations:**
- `|v|^(1/3)` is a very specific nonlinear function. None of the candidates contain `Abs(v)` or fractional powers of v.
- `t*x` is a product term. None of the candidates explicitly contain `t*x`.
- `tanh` can approximate linear functions for small arguments but is NOT exactly linear.
- `cos(sin(...))`, `exp(sin(...))`, `exp(x²)*sin(t)` are all fundamentally different basis functions.

Let me verify: Can any candidate produce both `|v|^(1/3)` and `t*x`?

**No candidate contains `|v|^(1/3)` or any fractional power of |v|.** This is a basis function that cannot be constructed from polynomials in v (like v, v², v³), tanh, exp, sin, cos, sqrt, log, or rational functions of v.

**No candidate contains `t*x`.** The term `t*x` requires explicit multiplication of t and x. Some candidates have `exp(c*x²)*sin(t)` which is not `t*x`. None have a direct `t*x` term.

Since the GT requires both `|v|^(1/3)` and `t*x` as basis functions, and these are linearly independent from all basis functions present in any candidate, **no candidate can match the GT**.

Let me do a quick scan to confirm none have these terms:

- Candidates 1-50: None contain `|v|^(1/3)` or `t*x` explicitly.
- `log(c8*exp(c9*v) + 1)` (Candidate 17) is a softplus, not `|v|^(1/3)`.
- `sqrt(c1 + x²)` (Candidates 36, 45, 48, 50) cannot produce `|v|^(1/3)`.

Every candidate is missing the `|v|^(1/3)` term, which is essential and cannot be zero (β = 0.2917 ≠ 0). Since this is a fixed GT constant, this term must be present.
